Education News

Outlying Areas

Hangzhou City Elementary Schools Fight for Independent Education Funds

Request to Designate Residential Housing Donations as Special Funds for Municipal Education

The Hangzhou City education funds have traditionally been incorporated into the municipal budget without specific designated funds. Consequently, education funding fluctuates with the city's overall financial gains and losses, lacking reliable guarantees. This hinders expansion plans like adding schools and classes. To address this deficiency, the principals of the city's elementary schools have proposed that only independent education funding can facilitate educational progress. Therefore, they have resolved to petition the municipal government to designate the Hangzhou City store and residential housing donations as special education funds. This would ensure that municipal education achieves substantial advancement.

Film Censorship Committee to Switch to Full-Time Members Next Year

The Film Censorship Committee, jointly formed by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education, currently consists of seven members. These members are assigned concurrently from within the ministries and receive salaries from their respective departments. The committee members receive only a monthly allowance of thirty yuan per person for transportation. The committee has over ten additional staff members, with annual expenses totaling several thousand yuan. Each film screening requires the attendance of all seven committee members, along with three instructors dispatched by the Central Propaganda Department. The approval of a film requires at least one instructor from the Central Propaganda Department to sign off. Following a proposal by a committee member to convert the committee to full-time membership (requiring members to be full-time, proficient in foreign languages, and have received higher education), the matter has been submitted to the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education for review. Sources indicate that representatives from both ministries recently met within the Ministry of Interior and have, in principle, accepted the reform. However, the change to full-time membership is contingent upon budget considerations, as the Committee's budget for the 22nd year does not include provisions for this. (Currently, the members assigned by both ministries are mostly foreign-educated students who have received higher education and are proficient in several languages, with monthly salaries ranging from three to four hundred yuan. If converted to full-time status, they would no longer receive salaries from their departments. Even at a minimum salary of three hundred yuan, the total for seven members would be over two thousand yuan per month.) Therefore, it has been decided that the rationale behind this decision, along with the qualifications and experience of the current members from both ministries, will be jointly reported to the Executive Yuan. It is said that this matter will be managed by the Central Propaganda Committee in the future.

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education Orders County Education Bureau Chiefs to Conduct Inspections in Rural Areas, Emphasizing Prompt Implementation

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education issued an order to all County Education Bureaus stating: "It has been found that inspections of rural education by the heads of education bureaus are crucial for promoting the development of education throughout the county. Orders have been issued to follow the regulations promulgated by the department and to implement them promptly, and to submit reports on the results of the inspections for review. Now that the second semester of this year has already begun, it is observed that very few bureau chiefs have complied with the regulations during the last semester. It is noted that the education bureau chiefs of Qingpu, Taicang, Yixing, and Qidong counties have all conducted two rural inspections and submitted two reports, demonstrating diligent work that deserves commendation to encourage others. The counties of Changshu, Kunshan, Jiangdu, Gaoyou, Baoying, Shanghai, Xinghua, and Gaochun have submitted reports and should continue to implement the policy. The remaining counties have only reported conducting rural inspections without submitting reports and should immediately expedite the submission of reports for review. There are also those who have neither complied with the order to conduct rural inspections nor provided an explanation, showing complete disregard, which is unacceptable. For now, a lenient warning is issued. Starting this semester, efforts must be made to implement the regulations and, upon completion of the inspections, reports must be submitted for review. If there is any disregard, strict disciplinary action will be taken upon discovery. Each should comply diligently."

The meeting was chaired by Yang Yun-zhong. (1) The following eleven individuals were approved as ordinary members: Chen Yi (Zoology), Chen Shi-chang (Physics), Chen Shi-ti (Zoology), Yang Kai-shen (Education), Huang Ru-qi (Mathematics), Zhang Ming-de (Physiology), Zang Yu-jin (Psychology), Yang Ru-ji (Physics), Xiong Zi-jing (Physics), Wei Pei-xiu (Physics), and Chu Sheng-lin (Physics). (2) The Chairman reported that society member You Huai-gao had pledged to donate one thousand dollars to the society's biological research fund, with four hundred dollars already received. (3) The Chairman reported that new officers had been elected for the American branch of the society, with Zhou Tian elected as President, Wu Da-you as Secretary, and Xiong Xue as Treasurer. (4) Bing Nong-shan proposed that the funds raised for the biological research institute were still far from the target amount and that the board of directors and society members should be encouraged to assist. It was resolved that the directors would be invited to a meeting to discuss the matter when the incoming president traveled south, and that all society members would be asked to assist.

Categorized Statistics of the Vocational Guidance Center's Activities Over the Years

Few Professional Talents Placed in Jobs

Most Guidance for Students Entering Higher Education

The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center of the China Vocational Education Society has been established for six years since its founding in September 1927. The following is a categorized statistical summary of its various activities:

Job Placement: 803 people in 1927, 1,286 people in 1928, 3,974 people in 1929, 6,203 people in 1930, 7,183 people in 1931, 7,179 people in 1932, and 7,981 people in 1933 (up to June), totaling 34,609 people. Among these 34,609 people, job placement accounted for 70%, vocational guidance accounted for 15%, and career changes accounted for 15%. Discussions with professional talents accounted for only 20% of the cases. This 20% indicates that finding a job is not difficult, but rather that there is a lack of specialized skills.

Guidance for Higher Education: 55 people in 1927, 549 people in 1928, 1,160 people in 1929, 2,140 people in 1930, 2,672 people in 1931, 1,549 people in 1932, and 1,422 people in 1933, totaling 9,547 people. Among these 9,547 people, university students accounted for 40%, middle school students accounted for 50%, and primary school students accounted for 10%, indicating that vocational guidance is most needed at the middle school level.

Personal Consultations: Including legal, health, and marital matters, 26 people in 1927, 58 people in 1928, 108 people in 1929, 198 people in 1930, 324 people in 1931, 350 people in 1932, and 363 people in 1933, totaling 1,428 people. The above statistics show a steady increase in the number of people receiving such consultations over the years. Those seeking vocational consultations mostly requested job placement.

Registration Qualifications: The qualifications of those who registered at the center are summarized as follows: 3,545 graduates from domestic and foreign universities, 2,473 graduates from vocational schools, 2,072 graduates from normal schools, 2,399 graduates from secondary vocational schools, 2,668 graduates from secondary schools, 1,852 students who attended but did not graduate from secondary schools, and 1,021 others, totaling 16,030 people. Among the registrants, graduates from domestic and foreign universities with special technical skills were the most numerous, while those who attended but did not graduate from secondary schools and lacked the ability to continue their education were the least numerous. Men accounted for 88.4% and women accounted for 11.6%. Among those successfully placed, the most common occupation was education, followed by commerce, industry, and public service. The most common positions were teachers, accountants, clerks, shop assistants, and trainees, followed by engineers, technicians, and ticket sellers.

Job Placement Success: The statistics for those successfully placed after registering are as follows: 810 school teachers, 510 government agency employees, 283 factory employees and apprentices, 391 store employees and trainees, 150 ticket sellers, and 72 others, totaling 2,216 people. The above statistics show that out of over 16,000 people who entrusted the center with job placement, over 2,200 were successfully placed, nearly two-tenths of the total.

Agency Services: The statistics for various services entrusted by other locations are as follows: 284 planning projects, 434 investigation projects, 72 talent examination projects, 1,963 talent scouting projects, and 2,496 talent testing projects. On average, there were over ten planning and investigation projects per month. The average number of talent scouting projects was thirty per month. In the early years of operation, the number of talent scouting projects was relatively small, but in recent years, it has been around fifty per month. The number of talent examination and testing projects, which are temporary in nature, has also been increasing year by year.

Other Guidance: 1,285 people received health guidance, 923 people received legal guidance, service guidance was provided 15 times, and vocational lectures were given 176 times. Service guidance was provided through discussion groups, with leaders and experts from various industries invited to speak. Each session attracted one to two hundred people. These discussion groups and lectures can be generally categorized as vocational training, with over a thousand people receiving training each year.

Published Books: The following books have been published: (1) Overview of Vocational Guidance Implementation, (2) Collection of Vocational Guidance Lectures, (3) Summary of Industry Conditions, (4) Beekeeping Guidance, (5) Chicken Raising Guidance, (6) Vocational Problems, (7) Performance Evaluation Methods, (8) South Seas Service Guide, (9) Higher Education Guide, (10) Higher Education and Employment Guidance, (11) Health and Legal Guidance, (12) Collection of Examination Questions, (13) Youth Vocational Guidance, (14) Youth Higher Education Guidance, (15) Youth Service Guidance, (16) Youth Reading Guidance, (17) Service Ethics, (18) The Road to Success for Youth, (19) Vocational Guidance, (20) The Mother of an Intelligent Child, (21) How to Get a Job, (22) Records of a Trip to the East.

Resignation of Shanghai County Education Bureau Director Shi She

Shi She, the Director of the Shanghai County Education Bureau, has served for six years since taking office in August 1927. During his tenure, he has organized educational property, improved school facilities, promoted universal compulsory education, expanded social education, and implemented agricultural education. Recently, he has also devoted much effort to the issue of relocation and the division of property between the city and the county. The progress made in Shanghai County's education is largely due to his efforts. Director Shi recently submitted his resignation to County Magistrate Pan due to poor health.

Hunan Social Education Investigation Commissioner Arrives in Shanghai

The Hunan Provincial Department of Education has been paying close attention to social education in recent years. It is currently preparing to establish a rural construction experiment center in the suburbs of Changsha, formulating a seven-year plan to effectively implement mass education. Last month, it sent Zhou De-ding to investigate social education in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. Zhou recently arrived in Shanghai and visited the Municipal People's Education Center, the Zoo, and the Library. Yesterday, he visited Shanghai County, first meeting with Director Shi She at the County Education Bureau, who reported on the general situation of social education in the county. He then visited the Yutang People's Education Center, the Zhuanqiao Agricultural Education Center, the Minhang People's Education Center, the Maqiao People's Education Center, and various social education institutions in Shanghai County. Impressed by Zhou's dedication to social education, having traveled from afar, he was presented with a calligraphy inscription to express comradeship. Zhou will leave Shanghai for Zhejiang in a day or two for further visits.

Huangdu Rural Teachers School Principal to Travel to Japan

Zhou Fo-hai, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education, recognizing the urgent need for the reorganization and implementation of rural education, has specially selected nine individuals with outstanding service in the education field and excellent academic qualifications, including Teng Song-shi, to study in Japan. Teng arrived in Shanghai yesterday to prepare for his trip abroad.

Shanghai University Has Resumed Classes

Shanghai Hubei-Mei University's middle school and university departments began registration on February 9th and 10th, according to the school calendar. Except for students on sick leave, all students arrived at school on time, and formal classes began on the 12th. To improve the university, the first faculty meeting of the spring semester was held on the evening of February 15th, and there was much discussion on issues related to teaching and management. It is also learned that Principal Liu is currently on his way back from the United States and is expected to arrive in Shanghai on March 6th. The School of Commerce in the city center has also been approved by the Ministry of Education to continue operations.

White Goose Painting School Opens

The White Goose Painting School on Avenue Edward VII in Shanghai is an art group with a long-standing reputation. Famous painters Chen Qiu-cao, Fang Xue-gu, and Pan Si-tong serve as key instructors. The school has excellent facilities and outstanding results, and enrollment has been very enthusiastic. The school aims to provide young people with artistic aspirations with excellent research opportunities for career advancement. Both daytime and evening classes, as well as correspondence courses, are still available. Register as soon as possible. The school's spring semester is confirmed to begin on the 19th of this month.

Business News

Although Financial Silver Prices and Exchange Rates Rise

The Foreign Exchange Market Initially Strengthens but Ultimately Remains Tight

Chinese Merchants and Banks Take Advantage of Low Prices to Cover Positions

According to foreign telegrams, London's major terms rose slightly, with the near term at 1.25 and the far term at 6.25. Silver prices for the forward market rose by 6.8 to 7.5%. The exchange rate of the British pound against the US dollar rose by 3.75%, and the exchange rate of the US dollar against the British pound rose by 3.875%. The exchange rate of the British pound against the French franc rose by 6 centimes, and the exchange rate of the US dollar against the French franc rose by 2.1 centimes. London's raw silk fell by one shilling and one penny. Commodity prices also rose. The foreign exchange market opened with the near-term selling price of British pounds at one shilling and four pence and seventy-five, and the US dollar at thirty yuan and a half, which was tighter by 0.0625 for the British pound and 0.0625 for the US dollar compared to the previous close. After the opening, news came that the US would form a committee to discuss silver prices. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation (HSBC) announced that the British pound had risen by 0.115, the US dollar had risen by 0.075, the French franc had risen by 0.12 francs, the Hong Kong dollar had fallen by 0.0125, the Indian rupee had risen by 0.025 rupees, the Singapore dollar had risen by 0.075, the German mark had risen by 0.0175, and the Philippine peso had risen by 1.5 yuan. The process gradually hardened, but Chinese merchants were still accumulating, and banks were also taking advantage of the low prices to cover positions. HSBC, Chase, and Joseon were making great efforts to accumulate. In the end, the market suddenly tightened. The near-term selling price at the noon close was one shilling and four pence and sixty-eight seventy-five for the British pound and thirty-five yuan and thirty-seven seventy-five for the US dollar, which was tighter by 0.0125 for the British pound and 0.0625 for the US dollar compared to the previous close. Chinese merchants such as Fu Chang were accumulating US dollars, while Cantonese merchants such as Yuan Xing Yong Da Lian were slightly selling. Over 200,000 yuan worth of US dollars were settled. Bullion Prices Rise by 0.0625

National News Agency, London, 17th - Bullion prices rose by 0.0625 in both the near and far terms. The near term was at 20 pence and 375, and the far term was at 20 pence and 4375. The British-American exchange rate opened at 5 yuan and 0.0925.

Several Announcements Regarding Gold Exchange Settlement Prices

The method for settling gold prices in April has been agreed upon. The Gold Exchange issued several announcements on February 10th. The main points were covered in the extra edition of this newspaper on the 13th. To provide readers with a comprehensive understanding, the original text is supplemented below:

(1) Revised Settlement for April: Due to the reduction in the weight of US gold coins starting from February 1st of this year, the trading methods for February and March have been announced to the market. All new transactions for April are scheduled to begin trading on the 20th of this month. The various methods for regular trading until the end of the period for settlement were consulted with the Brokers Association. The Association responded that they had convened a general meeting of brokers on the 7th of this month to discuss and pass the resolution. The various methods are listed below: (1) New transactions for April are scheduled to begin trading on February 20th and will be handled as follows: The gold content of current US gold coins is still 50%. Each yuan weighs 15.1381 grains, equivalent to 0.315971 li, which is 0.0284375 taels. (2) For all regular trading until the end of the period, if the goods have not been delivered, the settlement will be based on the initial US dollar exchange rate quoted by HSBC on that day, plus expenses, with 346 US dollars per bar.

(2) April Weights Changed to Market Standards: Following government orders, the new system of weights and measures will be used. All transactions at the exchange will uniformly switch to the market standard starting from February 10th. It is hereby announced that each market tael is equal to 0.8525 Cao taels.

(3) February and March will still be calculated using Cao taels: The purchase and sale of metals for the February and March periods will still be calculated using Cao taels, and the transaction price will also be based on Cao taels until the end of the period. From the beginning of new transactions in April, the transaction price will be based on market taels.

(4) Red Gold Settlement Changed to Customs Gold: Starting from February 20th, for all red gold sales at the exchange where the delivery date is specified, if the goods cannot be delivered at the appointed time, the settlement will be based on the initial customs gold price quoted by the Central Bank on that day, with 514 customs gold dollars per bar of 99% red gold. This is hereby announced. (Note: One customs gold dollar is equivalent to 0.019159 market taels. 514 customs gold dollars are equivalent to ten market taels of 99% red gold.)

Securities

Amidst Talk of Silver Price Revision

New York Bonds Speculatively Bought, Prices Rise

A report from the New Feng Foreign Firm on the 16th stated: The New York stock market was relatively stagnant. Towards the end, prices rose due to short covering. Exchange authorities sent questionnaires to various brokers, requesting truthful reports on recent transactions in aviation stocks. Consequently, the market entered a period of consolidation. Mining stocks were consistently strong throughout the day. Silver mining stocks initially rose but later eased. The price of large silver bars reached $0.46, the highest peak in four years, due to rumors in the American West and Shanghai that Washington would soon take action on silver. However, this claim could not be verified. Furthermore, a secretary of Roosevelt in Washington stated that he was unaware of anything. Nevertheless, reports indicated that the government was about to revise and increase the price of silver. Bond prices rose due to active speculative and investment buying. Daily trading volume reached 2.77 million shares. (Wheat) Market conditions were quiet, with all parties awaiting more accurate reports on harvest losses. (Cotton) Prices were firm due to successful reports of voluntary acreage reduction and supporters of the朋克海案(朋克海案, likely referring to a contemporary policy or legal case) predicted its implementation. The foundation was strong. Textile mills were calm, with factory purchases decreasing by 295,000 bales. The Dow Jones indices are listed below:

Cotton Yarn

Foreign Cotton Imports Decreased Last Year

Domestic Cotton Consumption Remains Good

Transactions Reached Over 266,000 Bales

Over 411,000 Bales of 通姚 Cotton Arrived at the Docks

Cash consumption of cotton in 1933 was good. According to market records, the annual total was 189,258 pieces (each piece weighing 500 pounds), equivalent to 266,108 bales (calculated at 120 catties per bale). Last year's foreign cotton imports were lower than the previous year, mainly due to the sluggish yarn market and a relatively abundant domestic cotton harvest. There are concerns that imports may gradually increase in the first half of this year, as華棉(華棉, likely refers to domestic cotton) inventories are becoming increasingly depleted. The government's subsidized purchase of American cotton is too expensive, with only tens of thousands of bales arriving in Shanghai, and a large batch has yet to be imported. Furthermore, the recent intense promotion of acreage reduction in the United States has intensified the upward trend in the cotton market. At the end of last year, spot "Middling" cotton rose from $0.1035 to a peak of $0.1265 on February 10th. Indian cotton prices were the first to rise due to the successful 中印 agreement. The price of 白洛區 cotton for April-May delivery rose from 174 rupees 25 to a peak of 115 rupees 5 on February 10th. The speed of the price surge in the overseas cotton market exceeded expectations. At the same time, the domestic market was also stimulated by foreign cotton prices, and because it was the end of the lunar year and rivers were frozen, transportation was difficult, and sources were depleted, triggering speculative purchases. In February, standard cotton rose from $39.75 on December 28th of last year to $44 on February 9th. At this time, market sentiment was extremely positive, as high foreign cotton prices made imports difficult and domestic cotton was insufficient to meet demand, resulting in a particularly favorable situation. However, the yarn market suffered from an unfavorable environment, and its rising power was weaker, resulting in sluggish factory sales. The future depends on the trends in foreign cotton. Dock arrivals of cotton throughout the year in 1933 totaled 267,511 bales of 姚花 and 143,783 bales of 通州花. A list of the transaction volumes and highest and lowest prices of spot cotton purchased by various factories throughout the year is provided below for reference:

[Silk and Tea]

European and American Silk Sales Progress Awaits

English Tussah Silk Experiences Sharp Rise British silk mills have already restricted the use of Japanese silk. As the demand for raw materials for spring silk fabrics increases, the Chinese silk market is showing improvement. Tussah silk prices have risen sharply, with Grade A 繡麟飛馬牌 (Embroidered Unicorn Flying Horse Brand) priced at 7 shillings 6 pence per pound and Grade B 黑獅牌 (Black Lion Brand) also at 7 shillings, both up by 6 pence. Calculated in Chinese currency, the price per bale has increased by 40 to 50 yuan.

Sichuan Silk Supply Disrupted The supply of Sichuan yellow silk has been scarce since last winter. In the past half month, shipments to Shanghai have been rare. Local Sichuan silk merchants recently received letters from producing areas stating that this is due to shallow water levels in the upper Yangtze River, making navigation difficult. Normal shipments will resume only after spring water levels rise.

Foreign Silk Market Inactive Due to Spring Holiday The local foreign silk market is inactive as foreign firms are closed for the Spring Festival holiday. They have not yet fully returned to work as of yesterday and will only resume business next Monday. Therefore, European and American silk sales have halted. Yesterday, only the Shanghai Silk Factory purchased 30 bales of yellow and white factory silk, and prices remained firm.

Grains

Large Quantities of Hankou Soybean Cakes Transferred to Shantou and Xiamen

Soybean cakes are considered the best fertilizer for Chinese farmers. They are produced in North China's Dalian and along the Yangtze River in Hankou, as well as in Qingkou and Haizhou in northern Jiangsu. In recent years, sales of soybean cakes have been slightly sluggish due to competition from imported chemical fertilizers. Chemical fertilizers are most widely sold in South China. However, starting last month, Shantou, Xiamen, and other places have been purchasing large quantities of soybean cakes, all from Hankou. Therefore, recently, ships arriving in Shanghai from Hankou have been carrying mainly soybean cakes for transfer to South China. It is reported that about 200,000 cakes have already been exported, and another 400,000 to 500,000 cakes are waiting to be loaded in Hankou for transshipment in Shanghai.

Hardware

Hardware Industry Profits Not Weak

The business situation of the hardware industry in 1933, viewed in the context of all industries, was still relatively satisfactory. Therefore, more companies made profits, and fewer closed down. Most goods were profitable in the first half of the year. In the second half of the year, due to the influx of Japanese goods, items such as plain sheet iron and new lead wire suffered slight losses. However, overall, substantial profits were still earned. According to investigations, the most profitable companies include Yuxianglong, Yidamao, Fengyong, Tongchang, Ruichang, Shunheng, Daxing, Xiangyuan, Chunyi, and Changchangji, totaling over ten companies. Their profits ranged from 120,000-130,000 to 30,000-40,000. The next tier includes Cheng Yu Hong, Chengtai Shun, He Rui Xin, Shun Xintai, Zhengji, Qiantai, Xiang Shun Kang Rui Da, totaling twenty to thirty companies. Their profits also ranged from 10,000-20,000 to 30,000-40,000. Furthermore, some companies have not yet finalized their accounts, or are keeping them secret, so details are not fully known. However, most companies made profits, and very few suffered losses.

Cotton Yarn

Golden Rooster Yarn Standard Still Difficult to Implement

Brokerage side is still not unified

Although it was previously rumored in the market that the Shanghai Yarn and Cloth Exchange would open the bidding for Golden Rooster Yarn as the standard on February 19th, some brokers were concerned about the interests of future operations and could not reach a consensus. Therefore, brokers convened another meeting on February 10th, but no practical solution was reached.

According to another source, although the board of directors has decided to proceed with the plan, the brokers have not fully approved it, so the new standard is unlikely to be launched on February 19th.

Children's Weekly Chun Qiu

Why Should We Study?

— Nan Cun

Little friends, why do you want to study? This is worth exploring. Think about it yourself. What is the reason?

People always have a purpose and a hope in doing anything. Following the purpose and hope, they move forward and gradually achieve satisfactory results. What is the purpose and hope of studying?

Mr. Wang Yangming, a great Confucian scholar of our country, had already clearly stated this question when he was a primary school student. I will tell you, please pay attention.

When Wang Yangming was very young, he was studying in a private school. He asked the teacher why he wanted to study. The teacher replied that studying would allow him to obtain fame and wealth. Wang Yangming said that this was not the case, it was for learning the methods of (being a person). The teacher greatly appreciated this. Later, Wang Yangming became a great Confucian scholar. It is truly rare that he had such insightful views at a young age.

Japan's national strength comes from Wang Yangming's doctrines (innate knowledge) and (unity of knowledge and action), and the Japanese themselves admit it. Wang Yangming was a virtuous man of our China in the past. We Chinese do not study his doctrines, and do not follow them, but instead the Japanese learn them. Is this not a strange tale? There is a book (Wang Yangming) in the children's books of the bookstore, you can buy a copy and read it to get a general idea. As for the complete works written by Yangming, you cannot understand them clearly now, and you cannot read so much. Wait until your level increases in the future, then study them!

As for how to be a person, what is said in the books you have read is all teaching you to do as they say. If the things you usually do feel very bad, and are inconsistent with the books, then you must change them. This is called (applying what you have learned).

That Day of School Opening

— Li

Today our school opened, and in the morning, I got up very early. After finishing breakfast, I immediately carried my books and went to school. On the way, I ran into many old classmates, so we ran into a large group, and everyone walked to school together. At this time, there was a lot of unspeakable joy in my heart.

After we entered the school, we saw many more classmates. They were smiling, shouting, and jumping. Everyone was wearing new clothes and was very happy.

Later, the bell rang ding-ding-dong, meaning that the school opening ceremony was about to be held. So all of us students, like waves, poured into the large auditorium.

After the various ceremonies were completed, our Principal took the stage to speak. It seemed that his voice always carried a smile. I stood on tiptoes to look over and saw his mouth moving slowly.

What Principal行(Principal Xing) was saying was (telling us to be good students, to study hard, not to play truant, to respect teachers, and to be as kind and loving to each other as our own brothers); and many other things, I can't remember them all at the moment.

In addition, there were also several teachers who took the stage to speak, and they also seemed very happy, always with smiling faces, their eyes looking at us one wink at a time.

Today the school is full of a new atmosphere. Today is the school opening, today is the happiest day for many teachers, and also the happiest day for many students, and also my happiest day!

Today, my mother also invited guests over, giving me many biscuits and candies. Today seems to be her happiest day too.

Dad Has

— Zui Zhu

Hezhen came back from school, threw down her schoolbag, and jumped and ran to her father, asking for ten copper coins, and took her ball to play at the door.

Far away, she saw Ah San from the cobbler's house and Ah Er, who collected cigarette butts, walking hand in hand and laughing happily at the entrance of the alley. Hezhen turned her head and pursed her lips. She thought: These two poor children are really annoying. The tactless Ah San shouted loudly behind her:

(Hey! Hezhen, do you have any copper coins?) Ah Er and Ah San sold the cigarette butts they had collected today and got ten copper coins. They came here specifically to show them to Hezhen.

(Yes! I have ten!) Hezhen suddenly turned around and stretched out her little hand, answering very proudly.

(We also have ten each!) Ah Er and Ah San also stretched out their black hands together, shouting triumphantly!

(You two only have ten: I alone have ten. And my dad has, do you have a dad who has?) Hezhen said angrily, wanting to outdo these two poor children.

Ah Er smiled lightly and said: (You rely on your dad, I rely on my hands. If your dad doesn't give you any, you won't have any);

Ah San also echoed with a smile (Sometimes a dad is not as good as a hand, it's most lasting to earn money with your own hands.)

The two of them, like singing a song of victory, clapped their hands, laughed, sang, and left. Before leaving, they also made a funny face to shame Hezhen.

At this time, Hezhen could only grumble to herself (Dad has! Dad has.)

The Structure of a Watch

— Zhen

Zhi'er is a bright and lively child, so in this autumn semester, he studied hard, and the report card sent by the school will certainly not be without progress, and he is ranked first in his grade. Teachers praised him, and parents loved him.

His parents happily bought him a watch as a reward for studying hard.

Zhi'er was very happy with his shiny pocket watch, often staring at it blankly, feeling that the hands on the watch face would move, and at the same time he heard the ticking sound, which was really wonderful.

He became curious again, and asked his brother, Huier, in surprise: (Brother, look! How do these three hands move? Listen! Why is there a ticking sound? Brother, can you answer me?)

Huier thought for a while and replied to him: (Little brother! The longest hand is called the minute hand: the short hand is called the hour hand: the shortest hand is called the second hand. Inside the watch are gears, a spring, and a hairspring. Each swing of the hairspring takes a certain amount of time, called the isochronism of the swing. Each swing is counted as one second. When it swings, it causes the gears to rotate, driving the hour and minute hands to indicate the time. The spring uses the elasticity of steel to keep the hairspring swinging continuously. The teeth around the gears mesh with the teeth of another gear. If one gear rotates, all the other gears also rotate. The ticking sound is the sound made when the hairspring is swinging. If you want to keep your watch from breaking forever, there are two ways: One, do not open the watch case often, to prevent dirt from entering, as the gears will gradually stop. Two, wind the spring tightly, and do it at a fixed time.)

Zhi'er happily hid the watch and went outside to play.

The Hunter and the Woodcutter

— Yin Lie

A hunter was searching for lion tracks in the mountains and forests. He met a woodcutter and asked him if he had seen any lion tracks, and if he knew where the lion was hiding. The woodcutter said:

(Hey, I can point out a live lion to you.) When the hunter heard this, his face turned pale and his teeth chattered. He said:

How to draw an elephant Two egg shapes and a tail Four legs and one ear Add some Oh, it's you!

(I just want to see the lion's tracks; I don't want to see a live lion.)

There are so many people in the world who are only brave in words and not brave in deeds, little friends! Do you want to be someone who is brave in deeds but reluctant to speak, or do you want to be someone who is brave in speaking but reluctant to do things?

Children's Jokes

— Qiu Lang

Thickest Skin

Brother: Do you know which part of the human body has the thickest skin?

Younger Brother: I think it's probably the face.

Brother: Why do you say that?

Younger Brother: Look at this cold weather, everyone is wearing cotton clothes, leather clothes, gloves, and cotton shoes, but only the face is not covered at all. Isn't that because the skin on the face is the thickest?

Clear at a Glance

Older Sister: Little sister, why do you always close one eye when you read?

Younger Sister: Because I heard people say: (clear at a glance), if you open both eyes, you can't see clearly.

Don't Tell Him

Passerby: Which of you two is the older brother? Which is the younger brother?

Ling'er: Brother: Don't tell him.

Small Experiences

— Jian Fen

Book Covering Paper

Little friends: The (books) you read are often placed on the desk, and the (covers) are easily dirtied, aren't they? The (cover) is like our own lovely (face). If our (face) is dirty, it would be unsightly, wouldn't it? So when you receive your (new books) at the beginning of the school year, quickly cover them with (book covering paper). This way, the ink stains and filth on the desk and hands won't easily get on the (cover). Because there is a layer of (book covering paper) outside the (cover). When you are on vacation and have finished reading the (books), and you are about to put the (books) away, take off the (book covering paper): Little friends, isn't the (cover) of this (book) still very new then?

Curling Book Corners

Little friends: Do the (corners) of your lovely (books) often curl up? If this happens, to avoid the (book corners curling) up, take active measures: | Before the (book corner) curls | When reading (books), don't lean your hands on the (book) and don't flip it over frequently. After reading, put the (book) in a (book clip). Take passive measures: | After the (book corner) has curled | First, straighten the curled (book corner) to its original shape, clip it in a (book clip), and press it flat with a heavy object. Second, correct the bad habit of (book corners curling).

Cold Shrinks, Heat Expands

— Zhi Yuan

Zhang'er heard the teacher say that all objects expand when heated and shrink when cooled. He also saw the teacher's experiment, using a small copper ball with a chain attached, placed on a small copper frame. The ball could move up and down through the hole in the frame. Later, the ball was heated over an alcohol lamp for some time and then placed on the frame, and the ball was held firmly. The teacher said: "This is because heat expands the object. The area of the ball has expanded after being heated by burning, so it can be held." After twenty minutes, the ball fell down again. The teacher said: "(This is because cold shrinks the object. Although the ball expands when heated, it shrinks back to its original shape after the heat dissipates, so it falls down again.)" Zhang'er understood the concept of thermal expansion and contraction very well.

One day, during a very cold winter, his tea glass broke because the tea inside froze overnight and filled the glass. His father said: "(When water freezes, its volume increases, so the glass broke. It's because you didn't pour out the tea inside last night)." Zhang'er said, "(Heat expands, isn't this an exception? Doesn't cold expand?)"

While eating, Zhang'er saw someone pick up a large piece of fish soup jelly with chopsticks and put it in the hot pot. After a moment, he looked around in the hot pot and said, "(Who ate my fish jelly that was being heated?)" His father said: "(Silly child, doesn't fish jelly turn into soup when heated? How could it still be there?)" Zhang'er said: "Who knew there was an exception where heat shrinks, and it shrunk to the point of disappearing!"

Chemical Games

— De Ling

Igniting with a Glass Rod

Jinghui said to Xuemei: "The school's fun fair is coming up soon! What kind of performance shall we prepare?" Xuemei thought for a moment and said: "I have an empty water bottle and a large copper coin here. I'll also ask my mother for some yarn and pour some alcohol into the bottle to make a homemade alcohol lamp. Please go to Mr. Qian and borrow a glass rod and ask for some lithium salt and concentrated sulfuric acid." After a while, Jinghui and Xuemei got everything they needed. Then Xuemei dipped the glass rod in some sulfuric acid, then in some lithium salt, and then touched the end of the glass rod to the alcohol lamp wick, and the alcohol lamp lit. Jinghui laughed: "Great! Let's do this experiment!"

Making Fire with Water

Zhaolin was a student with excellent character and learning. On the day of her graduation ceremony, she went to the chemistry lab and asked the nature teacher for a small piece of sodium, which she preserved well in kerosene. She also prepared a small basin, a glass tube, some very dry lecture papers, and a glass of hot water. After the ceremony, during the entertainment, she tore the paper into pieces in front of everyone, poured kerosene on the paper, hid the sodium under the paper, and placed it in the small basin. Then she used the glass tube to suck up some hot water and dropped it on the sodium. The sodium and water combined to form sodium hydroxide and released a high amount of heat, causing the sodium to burn, and thus the paper also burned. Everyone who watched was baffled.

Self-Igniting Fire

Wenshu took an empty ink bottle, poured some carbon disulfide into it, and cut some yellow phosphorus in water and put it into the carbon disulfide. The yellow phosphorus gradually dissolved, forming a solution of carbon disulfide and yellow phosphorus. One day, after the semester exams were over, when the class held a farewell party, Wenshu poured some of this solution onto paper and placed it on an iron tripod. In a short while, the paper started to emit white smoke, and then boom! The paper burned. The classmates were very surprised and didn't know what chemicals Wenshu used, they just clapped their hands non-stop.

Chemical Fire-Making

Shuming read about the method of making fire using chemicals, invented three hundred years ago, in the first volume of the Children's Science Series, in the chapter on matches. So she bought some white sugar and also found some lithium oxate and sulfuric acid. First, she carefully mixed equal amounts of sugar and potassium oxate. Then she took some and placed it on a wire mesh on an iron frame or on bricks. She used a glass rod to drip some sulfuric acid on the mixture, and immediately a bright flame burst out and burned. Shuming was very happy, but she didn't know that sugar is a carbohydrate, potassium oxalate contains a lot of oxygen, and sulfuric acid can absorb the water in the sugar and make it heat up, thus causing it to burn.

Making Fire on Ice

Lu Zhen's father was an old scholar from the Qing Dynasty who liked to smoke a water pipe. The north wind of the previous New Year had already blown the Siberian cold current to the Southern country. The water outside had hardened and formed crystal-like ice blocks. Lu Zhen hoped that his father would understand the progress of science, believe in the omnipotence of science, and to make his father happy, he secretly wrapped two small potassium sticks in the head of the water pipe and knocked a piece of ice from outside. With a naive smile and a round face, he said to his father, "Dad! I'm making fire on ice for you to smoke the water pipe!" As he spoke, he touched the potassium stick on the pipe head to the surface of the ice. Because the potassium reacted with the water, it produced fire, and the pipe head was lit.

There's no such easy thing,

If you commit a crime, don't think of escaping.

Telegraph Special Issue

Voice of the Telegraph World

Telegraphs and Roads (Part 1)

— Lü Bing

Notes for Telegraph Senders and Receivers

The transmission of telegrams has no relation to roads. However, the title of this article is "Telegraphs and Roads," so readers may suspect that telegraphs are involved in road construction or are used in conjunction with highways, air routes, railways, or automobiles. This is not the case. The route that telegrams travel can be called a "circuit," whether it is wired or wireless. When the circuit is open, the telegram can reach its destination. The "circuit" of a circuit and the "road" of a road are the same "road," but in reality, they cannot be confused.

If we place ourselves in the middle of a busy avenue and see vehicles coming and going, one after another, and also see police officers directing traffic and traffic lights indicating directions, each heading to their desired destination in an orderly manner without any confusion, we can reflect on this and infer that telegraphic communication is no different from road communication. Understanding the conditions of roads and using them to infer about telegraphs is more than halfway to understanding. Therefore, "Telegraphs and Roads" does not mean that telegraphs rely on roads. In fact, the sending, receiving, and traveling of telegrams can be compared to the conditions of roads. Telegraphs or roads? I can confidently say that by observing roads, you can understand telegraphs.

For telegraph senders and receivers, to understand the actual situation of telegraph transmission, one should first know the direct line that the telegram travels. The so-called direct line refers to the ability to send directly from one place to another, without bothering intermediate stations for retransmission. For example, Shanghai is directly connected to Nanjing, Tianjin, Hankou, and Fuzhou, and the message arrives as soon as it is sent. Therefore, even if the distance between Shanghai and the above-mentioned places seems quite far on the map, the time it takes for each telegram to reach the receiver from the sender is only a few minutes. This situation is analogous to a private car carrying passengers directly from one place to another without stopping along the way.

Based on our experience of traveling by car, the Beijing-Shanghai train first arrives at Wuxi and then reaches Nanjing. By analogy, it seems that telegrams sent to Wuxi should arrive faster than those sent to Nanjing. However, this idea is not entirely accurate, because telegraph transmission is divided into direct and non-direct routes. Therefore, telegrams from Shanghai to Wuxi usually take the route from Shanghai to Zhenjiang to Wuxi, with the Zhenjiang station handling the transfer. As a result, it cannot be as fast as telegrams from Shanghai to Zhenjiang or Beijing to Shanghai. This is like taking a car to a place that does not have a direct stop, and you often have to get off near the destination and make a detour. Observing how the road stops are divided is no different from the regulations of circuits. (Someone may wonder, why can't circuits be opened for direct access everywhere? This belongs to a business problem. Direct routes are beneficial for busy operations. If the operations are light, direct lines are permanently occupied, which is not economical.)

Benefits of the Account-Based Telegram Guarantee Method

— Zhen

Implemented from March 1st

Previously, in order to facilitate telegram sending for various businesses, telegraph offices and radio stations allowed them to deposit an approximate amount of monthly telegram fees in advance. At the end of the month, the accounts were settled, and any overpayment was refunded, and any underpayment was made up. This was called "pre-depositing telegram fees." However, this method was managed independently by each office and station, and there was no regulation. The deposited funds and interest were not reported to the Ministry of Communications, so the Ministry could not audit them. The interest on the deposited funds was not given to the businesses, causing them to suffer losses. In some cases, the funds deposited last year had not yet been settled this year, or the funds collected by the previous director of the office or station had been taken away, and the current director denied them because there was no case to audit. This has been a long-standing practice, and both businesses and offices/stations have suffered from it. Now, the electrical administration authorities have recognized this problem and have formulated eleven articles of the Account-Based Telegram Guarantee Method, which have been ordered to be implemented by all offices and stations from March 1st. The main points of the articles and the benefits for both parties are described below:

(1) Regarding the business side:

1. The purpose of a business sending telegrams is to have the telegrams transmitted quickly to their destination, which benefits their business. However, to achieve this goal, there must be a premise, that is, the telegram receiving procedure must be very simple. Therefore, the principle of pre-depositing telegram fees is indeed adoptable. Now, to be cautious about telegram fees, it is stipulated that any business that applies to send account-based telegrams should deposit the approximate amount of monthly telegram fees in cash with the office/station's bank as a telegram fee guarantee. The amount of the guarantee is fixed and does not change. Account-based telegram fees are paid monthly and are not deducted from the guarantee to avoid the trouble of rolling calculations. Thus, businesses not only have the convenience of sending account-based telegrams but also have the right to verify their deposited funds. This is the fundamental difference between the Account-Based Telegram Guarantee Method and pre-depositing telegram fees. This is the first benefit.

2. According to the provisions of Article 3 of the method: "(The guarantee is deposited in the bank, and the office/station may not withdraw it unless one of the following situations occurs: (a) The business fails to pay the telegram fees due, and the office/station withdraws the telegram fees; (b) The business stops sending telegrams, and the office/station withdraws the funds for payment; (c) The business reduces the number of telegrams sent, and the office/station withdraws the funds to return part of the guarantee." With such clear regulations, it is impossible for unscrupulous handlers to touch this money. Thus, businesses do not have to worry about the unauthorized withdrawal of the guarantee, and the office/station does not have to worry about the lack of telegram fees. There is mutual guarantee and mutual trust, which is the second benefit.

3. The interest on the guarantee is calculated by the bank every six months, and the office/station allocates it to the business that deposited the funds. Thus, the interest on the business's deposited funds will definitely not be lost. This is the third benefit.

4. Article 8 of the method states: "(If the business reduces the number of telegrams sent, it may request the office/station to return part of the guarantee.)" Thus, although the guarantee is deposited in the bank, if the business does not need to send many telegrams, it can still request the return of part of the guarantee. This is not like the previous pre-deposited telegram fees, even if they are withdrawn. This is the fourth benefit.

5. Article 9 of the method has the provision that "(the guarantee may be replaced by a guarantee letter from a bank designated by the office/station)," which is even more convenient. Most of the telegram senders in various places are financial institutions, or they have a considerable relationship with financial institutions. Now that the guarantee can be replaced by a guarantee letter from a bank designated by the office/station, the business only needs to obtain a letter from the bank to obtain the qualification to send account-based telegrams. Why not do it?

(2) Regarding the office/station side:

1. Simple telegram receiving procedures: When telegrams are sent to the receiving and sending department of the office/station, the receiving staff must calculate the number of words, calculate the telegram fee, issue a receipt, and find the change, etc. This procedure takes at least three minutes. If there are ten senders arriving at the office at the same time, the last telegram will be delayed by thirty minutes. If the account-based telegram method is adopted, the receiving staff only needs to sign in the telegram sending book, which is enough. The remaining procedures can be done after the telegram is transmitted. Then the speed of the telegram must be greatly increased.

2. Telegram fees will not be empty: After the guarantee is deposited in the bank, the office/station may not withdraw it unless one of the three situations mentioned above (a, b, and c) exists. Thus, even if the supervisor wants to use the money temporarily, it is impossible. Therefore, the act of filling one's own pocket with the deposited funds is impossible in fact. The procedures for settling telegram fees and deducting the guarantee, and the recovery of telegram fees exceeding the guarantee, are separately and strictly regulated by Articles 6 and 7 of the method. Therefore, there is no worry that telegram fees will be empty.

The purpose of depositing money to send telegrams is to facilitate businesses and the public. If there is no definite method, greedy people will regard it as a source of profit, which will not only damage the reputation of the office/station but also harm business and seek private gain, which violates the prohibited laws. Now, the electrical administration authorities have stipulated an Account-Based Telegram Guarantee Method, which sweeps away the long-standing bad habits of the past. This is indeed a gratifying move. If various businesses go to the office/station to try it out, they will know that I am not deceiving them.

Overview of the Bypath Automatic Telephone

— Jin

Installed in the Advances Telephone Exchange

The Advances Telephone Exchange in the United Kingdom opened on February 23, 1933. The opening ceremony was performed by the former Postmaster General, Mr. Etherly. This is the first time in the world of telephones that the Bypath automatic telephone was used. All the components, except for the electrical part, were made by Stsndard Telephones and Cables Ltd. This type of machine was developed by an engineer who participated in the European War as part of the Royal Communications Corps. He continued to study it at the company's Hendon Testing Center for seven years before the exchange was installed. This automatic telephone was purely at the request of the company, and the Post Office was not under any obligation. However, for trial purposes, it was allowed to be installed two years ago. In the four months before the opening, it was tested in detail by engineers from the Post Office. The exchange currently has a capacity of 3,400 subscribers and can be expanded to 10,000 in the future. The selector used is only a horizontal rotary type, which is simple and saves costs. According to the business manager of the company, who told the press, this type of machine is 20% cheaper than the Strowger System machine, occupies 30% less area, weighs 40% less, saves 10% on electricity, saves 29% on the connecting wires between the various levels of selectors, and can also reduce maintenance costs. Judging from the various advantages, it is believed that many people will adopt it in the future. This type is not only suitable for use in large cities, but also for small rural exchanges that are unmanned. The advantages and equipment are outlined below:

(1) Advantages of the Bypath system

The advantage of the Bypath automatic telephone is that it occupies very few components when two subscribers are talking. In other automatic telephones, expensive and complex selectors are usually used to select the number. And from the time the number is selected until the call is completed, it is always occupied, and other users cannot use it. The attached relays and parts, even if one part of them is only used to select the number and is not needed during the call, must also be occupied. However, this type is different. All number selection work is done step by step by another part of the Bypath selector. Once selected, the wire is immediately removed for use by other subscribers. Therefore, the parts that are occupied but not used during the call can be reduced. The circuit of each level of selector can be simple. Some only have one relay. The number of machine components is therefore reduced. Each set of Bypath selectors is composed of several horizontal rotary selectors and several relays. The number of Bypath selectors required for the entire exchange is not large. Each set of Bypath selectors can be used for ten subscribers to call. The attached diagram shows the operation of the various levels of components when calling a five-digit number. (To be continued)

Four Hundred Thousand

— Guan

The telegraph has implemented a price reduction. Names and addresses with fifteen characters are counted as five characters for billing. According to people in the telegraph industry, the Ministry of Communications created this new method. If the telegraph service is still the same as before, comparing income, the annual loss is about 400,000 yuan. This 400,000 yuan, which the Ministry loses, is naturally the benefit of the senders.

Let's think further. For example, after the telegram business reduces prices, it develops accordingly. The number of increased revenue is enough to offset the 400,000 yuan. Then, for the 400,000 yuan in revenue, all the telegraph offices and stations in the country, still following the practice of reducing fees for names and addresses, and not counting the report header, must receive at least about six million more words of telegrams than in previous years. How much electricity is consumed? How much material (including paper strips, ink, receiving and forwarding paper, etc.) is consumed? Although the reporter does not have time to make precise statistics, the number should be quite a bit.

Thinking about the work involved, increasing the number of words received and sent by six million means that two million four hundred thousand more telegraph codes need to be transmitted and copied, assuming each word is four codes. Also, if each code averages three dots and dashes, then the duty officers increase the number of dots and dashes of telegraph symbols transmitted to a total of seventy-two million! Although this is for the whole country, the number of words in the report header and the number of characters at the intermediate stations have not been counted, so in reality, it is definitely more than this.

Please try to imagine this, social figures, don't underestimate this telegram price reduction!

How to Use Social Telegrams

— Qinghua

Telegrams are very common communication tools, like express mail in the eyes of foreigners, and they are not considered particularly rare. However, in our country, where people's intelligence has not yet developed, the average person thinks telegrams are almost ominous things because they use them so rarely. Because receiving a telegram is not reporting the serious illness or bad news of family members or friends, but other troubles have occurred. You won't receive a telegram for something good. Under these circumstances, it is natural that the telegraph business cannot be fully developed!

Recently, the Ministry of Communications has seen this weakness, so it added a kind of social telegram to give the general public the opportunity to try to use telegrams. For just a few cents of telegram fee, you can send a telegram to relatives and friends, and the telegram text is not necessarily reporting ominous things, such as congratulating on a wedding, birthday, birth of a child, etc., making the telegram a lucky thing. Gradually create a trend in the minds of the public, only knowing that telegrams are the fastest communication tool. If there is an important matter, such as mail that can't make it in time, use a telegram. If relatives and friends have weddings or funerals, send a social telegram to congratulate or offer condolences, saving yourself the time of writing a long letter to congratulate or offer condolences, and also saving the recipient the time of reading the letter. And telegrams are always more valuable than mail, so the recipient will pay special attention to the telegram. If you want to express special feelings to relatives and friends, or, to be frank, if you want to please the other party, then you must use telegrams. Now, I will talk about how to use social telegrams, hoping that everyone is happy to use them and get the benefit of (spending a small fee and receiving great results).

(1) When the following kinds of things happen, you should use social telegrams to congratulate relatives and friends and express your good feelings: (1) Relatives and friends get married (2) Relatives and friends' birthdays (3) Relatives and friends give birth to children or grandchildren (4) Relatives and friends are promoted (5) Relatives and friends graduate or receive degrees (6) Relatives and friends' businesses are profitable or awarded prizes (7) Relatives and friends go abroad or return home (8) Colleagues open (9) Military victory over the enemy (10) Relatives and friends invent new things (11) Ceremonies such as highway opening, ship launching, airplane naming, and house completion (12) Christmas and New Year (13) Relatives and friends are elected to important positions (14) Athletes win or set new records (15) Other things that can be congratulated.

(2) When the following kinds of things happen, you should immediately send social telegrams to offer condolences to relatives and friends and express your sympathy: (1) Relatives and friends themselves or their family members get sick (2) Relatives and friends themselves or their family members die (3) Relatives and friends themselves or their family members temporarily encounter accidents, such as theft, kidnapping, fire, injury, being falsely accused or arrested, etc. (4) Funerals or anniversary of the deaths of relatives and friends' family members (5) Group strikes or dissolutions (6) Earthquake or other natural disasters (7) Places are ravaged by enemies or bandits (8) Relatives and friends' businesses are unsuccessful (9) Relatives and friends fail to get elected (10) Other things that should be consoled or condoled.

(3) When you receive a social telegram of congratulations or condolences from relatives and friends, you should immediately send a return telegram to express your gratitude. This return telegram is also considered a social telegram.

The above-mentioned method of using social telegrams is not simply for me to promote the telegraph office and attract business, but to advocate for the public to use telegrams to socialize with relatives and friends. If you socialize well in peacetime, your relatives and friends will be happy to help you, and it will be easy to succeed in whatever you want to do. So I dare say that using social telegrams is like sowing the seeds of success. To go a step further, social telegrams are success telegrams. Anyone who has always had a broad social circle must send social telegrams! People who don't send social telegrams cannot be considered to have a broad social circle! At the same time, people who have weddings or funerals must receive dozens or hundreds of social telegrams on the day of the event, which is considered a broad social circle and a full face!

One more thing, when relatives and friends whose friendship is not very deep send wedding invitations or obituaries, giving a gift that is too heavy seems unworthy, and a gift that is too light will not satisfy the recipient very much. If you switch to using social telegrams, it can make the recipient feel happy, and in fact, the cost is simpler. It is really (killing two birds with one stone!)

In addition, I hope that the telegraph office can deliver social telegrams at the time specified by the sender. For example, if the recipient is getting married at 4:00 p.m. on a certain afternoon, the sender can request that it be delivered at 4:00 p.m. on that afternoon, so that the recipient feels particularly gratified. Because delivering it too early or too late loses the timeliness of the telegram. This designated time can be written after the telegram text and signature, such as (1600), representing 4:00 p.m., which is counted as one character. If the distance is far, you can add a date, represented by a rhyme or code, also counted as one character.

Recent Developments in Wireless Telephone Technology in Various Countries (Part 2)

— Translated by Wang Dachun

The advance of Ultra Short Wave or MicroRay wireless telephones into practical use has been the greatest success in the transportation sector in recent years. It uses extremely short radio waves to transmit to distant locations without attenuation, echo, distortion, or other drawbacks. Furthermore, due to the shorter wavelengths, it can maintain communication secrecy, making it invaluable for military and other transportation purposes. This type of ultra-shortwave wireless telephone was first demonstrated between Dover in England and Calais in France on March 31, 1931. Now, it is in practical use and has reached a very perfected state. This demonstration used a two-way system with a wavelength of 18 centimeters (18c.m.) and an antenna of only two centimeters. During the demonstration, each location had over thirty listeners who used this telephone to communicate across the Strait of Dover. The results showed that such wavelengths do not attenuate as easily as ordinary radio waves and are less susceptible to absorption by rain or fog. Another advantage is that in ordinary wireless telephone transmitters, the wavelengths of each transmitter must be uniform. However, with ultra-shortwave telephones, the wavelength of each of the ten thousand transmitters can be different, yet effective transmission can still be achieved, accounting for about a quarter of the total.

Between 1930 and 1931, the British International Telegraph and Telephone Experimental Institute, in conjunction with the French Telephone Materials Experimental Institute, publicly tested a single sideband system for radio telephones used on short waves. The results clearly demonstrated that this type of wireless telephone had evolved to a commercially viable stage for shortwave communication. On May 21, 1931, in Madrid, the capital of Spain, and Trappes near Paris, this wireless telephone was publicly demonstrated. At that time, about seventy listeners listened to both sides communicating in English and French, and a special signal was demonstrated for about an hour, with excellent results. As for the spread sideband system applied to shortwave wireless telephones, there has also been progress, to the extent that it can completely eliminate or reduce the distortion caused by radio wave attenuation.

Mobile transportation tools, such as giant ships sailing in the ocean, are now equipped with wireless telephones, allowing passengers on board to have direct conversations with any telephone user in major cities in Europe and America. The wireless telephone of the Canadian Pacific Railway Company's mail ship (Empress of Britain) was installed early and could directly communicate with landline telephones. Telephone services in various parts of the United States have been connected to the wireless telephones of Furness Company's mail ship (Monarch of Bermuda) and (S.S Belgenland). When these ships were operating on world routes, there were several high-record transoceanic calls: First, the great scientist Albert Einstein and other celebrities used this telephone to broadcast nationwide from the pier in New York. The second was from the Pacific coast of Central America, with significant results. Other wireless telephone connections include direct lines from our country's territorial waters to the United States, Bombay to London, the Red Sea to the United States, and Alexandria in Egypt to Washington, D.C., all of which have recently opened. (End)

Semi-Monthly News

— Member of the Society

Revisions to the Telegraph Registered Address Regulations

The Ministry of Communications recently revised the current telegraph registered address regulations because they were established by the old Ministry of Communications and have been in use for nearly a decade, making them unsuitable for the current situation. The new regulations took effect on April 1 of this year. The important points of the new regulations are summarized below:

(1) Telegraph registered addresses only need to be registered at one telegraph office or radio station and can be used at both. (For example, Shanghai has six locations, including the telegraph office, domestic radio station, international radio station, and Sanshui line receiving and dispatching office. Registration only needs to be done at the joint registration office located in the telegraph office, and it will be valid at all locations.)

(2) Chinese and foreign registered addresses can be used interchangeably. (Under the old regulations, Chinese telegraphs were not allowed to use foreign registered addresses.)

(3) There are three types of registration: 1. Three years for 25 yuan; 2. One year for 10 yuan; 3. One month for 1 yuan. The effective period for three-year and one-year registrations is calculated from January 1 to the end of the year for registrations made in the first half of the year, and from July 1 to June 30 of the fourth or second year for registrations made in the second half of the year. One-month registrations are calculated uniformly from the first day of the month of registration to the end of the month. This registration can be applied for several months at a time. (Registrations that are about to expire can be re-registered according to the new regulations after the expiration date.)

The above two points are extremely beneficial to the public sending telegrams. The third point, the registration fee is calculated on a monthly or yearly basis, which seems slightly disadvantageous, but those who register for a long-term of three years can save as much as five yuan. All long-term businesses can benefit from this. Also, those who wish to register for a long-term registration in March-April or August-September can first register for a short-term for several months and then register for a long-term at the end of June or the end of the year to reduce the loss.

Telegraph Bureau to Notify Recipients of Prepaid Reply Telegrams

For the convenience of senders and receivers, the Telegraph Bureau has a method for senders to prepay the reply telegram fee so that the recipient can reply immediately after receiving the telegram without having to pay. However, many of our people are still not very clear about this method, so very few people use it. Even those who use it often have recipients who do not understand the situation and delay replying, causing the sender to wait anxiously, thinking that the Telegraph Bureau has delayed the telegram or failed to notify the recipient, causing a lot of misunderstandings. In order to be thorough, the Ministry of Communications has specially instructed all bureaus and stations to add a stamp on the bottom of the telegram for such telegrams: "This telegram has been prepaid for the reply telegram fee by the sender. Please bring the attached reply telegram voucher to the bureau to send the reply telegram." This is to make the recipient pay attention. If the telegram is not replied within three days after delivery, the bureau or station will send a letter to inquire again to avoid forgetting.

Long-Distance Telephone Bureaus and Offices Sell Telephone Directories

If local telephone subscribers in areas with long-distance telephone service need telephone directories from telephone bureaus or commercial telephone companies in other places, they can request the local telephone bureau or commercial telephone company to purchase them on their behalf. The Ministry of Communications has recently notified all telephone bureaus and commercial telephone companies to follow this method.

A Discussion on Cooperation Between the Telecommunications and Press Circles

— Ye Zhonghua

The level of a nation's culture is often judged by the development of its press.

And to assist the development of the press, telecommunications have a deep relationship. After all, the transmission of news cannot be done without relying on telecommunications as a powerful tool. All trends in the politics and economy of the world, as well as changes in natural disasters and human affairs, rely on telecommunications to transmit and present to our eyes in an instant. To run a newspaper without the records of telecommunications is to depreciate its own value; and for telecommunications not to be able to provide the use of news transmission is to fail to fulfill its duty to serve society. Therefore, the telecommunications industries of all countries in the world, whether state-run or not, do their best to cooperate and assist the press in various ways, because newspapers are the voice of the people and the guide of public opinion. Assisting the press is to maintain culture.

Since the establishment of telegraphs in our country, the transmission of news has followed the precedents of various countries around the world, giving the press various conveniences. Such as reducing the price of news telegrams and implementing the recipient-pays system, all of which are special rights enjoyed by the press. In recent years, although personnel salaries have increased and the price of machine parts and materials has risen, and the expenses of telecommunications administration have increased year by year. However, the transportation authorities, in these difficult circumstances, still try to reduce the burden on the press. For example, since January 1 of this year, all urgent news telegrams have been charged as ordinary telegrams, which is one example.

In recent years, the press in our country has become increasingly prosperous. Morning and evening newspapers are published day and night. The demand for news is strong, and the sending of news telegrams has become more frequent. Telegraph bureau staff pay great attention to the transmission of news telegrams. Generally, they must be completed before the newspaper is printed, so that the telegrams of the day can be published. This spirit of service is indeed the duty of the telegraph bureau. It is also that telegraphs and news are working together for culture, and since they have a common mission, they are willing to cooperate to the end.

The telegraph bureau's cooperation with the press is as mentioned above. However, there is one thing that is most unpleasant for the press, and that is news censorship. The government's purpose in setting up censorship is nothing more than to prevent the conspiracy of those who fabricate rumors and stir up trouble, and it is not a harsh treatment for the press. However, the telegraph bureau knows the pain of the press, so it strives to simplify and speed up the procedures for checking telegrams, so that news telegrams are not delayed by censorship. This fact should be well known to the press and understood by the press.

Finally, what we hope from the press is: in recent years, the telegraph business has been determined to reform, especially to reduce the price of telegrams, so as to meet the needs of society, such as the creation of low-cost social telegrams, the revision of the method of calculating the number of words in the recipient's name and address, and the reduction of the price of urgent telegrams, free inquiries of official telegrams, etc., all of which are to reduce the burden on senders and receivers. The Ministry of Communications has therefore reduced its revenue by about 500,000 yuan per year. This extraordinary reform is to enable society to fully use telegrams as a communication tool, so that the telegraph bureau can obtain more service opportunities. However, the implementation of this price reduction method cannot attract the attention of society without extensive publicity. Therefore, the most important task at present is how to awaken the public to develop the habit of sending telegrams, which depends on the cooperation and guidance of the press.
